This may not be the case for blocks containing\n    68→     nested functions, since we may actually call such a function even\n    69→     though the BLOCK information is messed up.  Defaults to true.  */\n    70→  bool (* ignore_block) (const_tree);\n    71→\n    72→  /* Record a source file location at (FILE, LINE, COLUMN, DISCRIMINATOR).  */\n    73→  void (* source_line) (unsigned int line, unsigned int column,\n    74→\t\t\tconst char *file, int discriminator, bool is_stmt);\n    75→\n    76→  /* Record a source file location for a DECL_IGNORED_P function.  */\n    77→  void (* set_ignored_loc) (unsigned int line, unsigned int column,\n    78→\t\t\t    const char *file);\n    79→\n    80→  /* Called at start of prologue code. It is part of the late\n   111→     debug pass and is called from rest_of_handle_final.\n   112→\n   113→     Location information is available at this point.\n   114→\n   115→     See the documentation for early_global_decl and late_global_decl\n   116→     for other entry points into the debugging back-ends for DECLs.  */\n   117→  void (* function_decl) (tree decl);\n   118→\n   119→  /* Debug information for a global DECL.  Called from the parser\n   120→     after the parsing process has finished.\n   121→\n   122→     This gets called for both variables and functions.\n   123→\n   124→     Location information is not available at this point, but it is a\n   125→     good probe point to get access to symbols before they get\n   126→     optimized away.\n   127→\n   128→     This hook may be called on VAR_DECLs or FUNCTION_DECLs. It is up\n   143→     to the hook to use what it needs.  */\n   144→  void (* late_global_decl) (tree decl);\n   145→\n   146→  /* Debug information for a type DECL. (It's not a boolean for\n   151→     legacy reasons.)  */\n   152→  void (* type_decl) (tree decl, int local);\n   153→\n   154→  /* Debug information for imported modules and declarations.  */\n   155→  void (* imported_module_or_decl) (tree decl, tree name,\n   156→\t\t\t\t    tree context, bool child,\n   157→\t\t\t\t    bool implicit);\n   158→\n   159→  /* Return true if a DIE for the tree is available and return a symbol\n   160→     and offset that can be used to refer to it externally.  */\n   161→  bool (* die_ref_for_decl) (tree, const char **, unsigned HOST_WIDE_INT *);\n   162→\n   163→  /* Early debug information for the tree is available at symbol plus\n   164→     offset externally.  */\n   165→  void (* register_external_die) (tree, const char *, unsigned HOST_WIDE_INT);\n   166→\n   167→  /* DECL is an inline function, whose body is present, but which is\n   168→     not being output at this point.  */\n   169→  void (* deferred_inline_function) (tree decl);\n   170→\n   171→  /* DECL is an inline function which is about to be emitted out of\n   172→     line. debug information generation chain consists of multiple layers that work together to produce debug information in DWARF format.\\n\\n## Debug Hooks Interface (gcc/debug.h and gcc/debug.cc)\\nThe entry point is the gcc_debug_hooks structure in gcc/debug.h (line 28-210), which defines a set of function pointers called by the front-end during compilation. These include hooks for initializing debug output (init), finishing it (finish), and processing individual language constructs. The gcc/debug.cc file provides default no-op implementations of these hooks.\\n\\n## DWARF Hook Implementation (gcc/dwarf2out.cc)\\nThe dwarf2_debug_hooks structure (gcc/dwarf2out.cc line 2893) implements the debug hooks interface for DWARF output. Key hooks include:\\n\\n- dwarf2out_init (line 30171): Initializes DWARF output structures\\n- dwarf2out_early_global_decl (line 27788): Processes global declarations early in compilation\\n- dwarf2out_late_global_decl (line 27883): Processes global declarations after optimization\\n- dwarf2out_function_decl (line 28239): Processes function declarations\\n- dwarf2out_source_line (line 29183): Records line number information\\n- dwarf2out_finish (line 32814) and dwarf2out_early_finish (line 33599): Complete debug generation\\n\\n## DIE (Debug Information Entry) Creation\\nThe core of debug information consists of DIE structures. The die_struct is defined in gcc/dwarf2out.cc (lines 3146-3175) and typedef'd as die_node (line 3175). Each DIE represents a language construct (type, variable, function, etc.).\\n\\nDIEs are created by new_die() (gcc/dwarf2out.cc line 5863) and new_die_raw() (line 5850). The new_die function allocates a die_node structure, sets its tag (DW_TAG_*), and links it into the DIE tree by calling add_child_die().\\n\\nAttributes are added to DIEs via add_dwarf_attr() (gcc/dwarf2out.cc line 4497) and various specialized functions like add_AT_flag, add_AT_string, add_AT_die_ref, etc.\\n\\n## Compilation Unit Structure (gcc/dwarf2out.h)\\nThe gcc/dwarf2out.h header file defines key types:\\n- dw_die_ref (line 25): Typedef for pointer to die_struct\\n- dw_attr_node: Attributes attached to DIEs\\n- dw_val_node: Values for attributes (strings, integers, references, locations, etc.)\\n\\n## Generation Functions\\nThe gen_* family of functions in gcc/dwarf2out.cc create DIEs for different language constructs:\\n\\n- gen_decl_die() (line 27537): Generates DIEs for declarations (variables, functions, types)\\n- gen_type_die() (line 27004) and gen_type_die_with_usage() (line 26764): Generate DIEs for types\\n- gen_subprogram_die() (line 23937): Generates function/subprogram DIEs\\n- gen_type_die_for_member() (line 23634): Generates DIEs for class/struct members\\n\\nThese functions call each other recursively to build complete debug information structures, emitting DIEs for nested types, parameters, and local variables.\\n\\n## Line Number Table Emission\\nLine number information is handled by:\\n\\n- dwarf2out_source_line() (line 29183): Records source line/column information for instructions\\n- dw_line_info_table (line 3061): Data structure holding line number entries\\n- dw_line_info_entry (line 3055): Individual line number records\\n- output_line_info() (line 13137): Emits the complete .debug_line section\\n- output_one_line_info_table() (line 12982): Emits individual line info tables\\n\\nThe line number table uses DWARF line number program opcodes to efficiently encode source locations.\\n\\n## Assembly Output (gcc/dwarf2asm.cc and gcc/dwarf2asm.h)\\nThe dwarf2asm module provides low-level assembly output functions:\\n- dw2_assemble_integer() (line 47): Outputs DWARF values as assembly\\n- dw2_asm_output_data(): Macro for outputting DWARF data with labels\\n\\nThese functions are called throughout dwarf2out.cc to emit the actual DWARF sections to the assembly file.\\n\\n## Alternative Output Formats\\nBuilt on top of DWARF DIEs are alternative debug formats:\\n\\n- gcc/dwarf2ctf.cc/h: Generates CTF (Compact C Type Format) and BTF (BPF Type Format) from DWARF DIEs via ctf_do_die()\\n- gcc/dwarf2codeview.cc/h: Generates Microsoft CodeView debug format from DWARF DIEs\\n\\n## Compilation Flow\\nThe complete chain works as follows:\\n1. Front-end calls debug hooks during compilation (via gcc_debug_hooks)\\n2. dwarf2out_early_global_decl/late_global_decl process declarations at appropriate times\\n3. gen_decl_die and related functions create DIE trees for all declarations\\n4. dwarf2out_source_line records line number information for code locations\\n5. output_line_info emits the .debug_line section with line number tables\\n6. dwarf2out_finish writes all remaining DWARF sections (.debug_info, .debug_abbrev, .debug_str, etc.)\\n7. point is the gcc_debug_hooks structure in gcc/debug.h (line 28-210), which defines a set of function pointers called by the front-end during compilation. These include hooks for initializing debug output (init), finishing it (finish), and processing individual language constructs. The gcc/debug.cc file provides default no-op implementations of these hooks.\\n\\n## DWARF Hook Implementation (gcc/dwarf2out.cc)\\nThe dwarf2_debug_hooks structure (gcc/dwarf2out.cc line 2893) implements the debug hooks interface for DWARF output. Key hooks include:\\n\\n- dwarf2out_init (line 30171): Initializes DWARF output structures\\n- dwarf2out_early_global_decl (line 27788): Processes global declarations early in compilation\\n- dwarf2out_late_global_decl (line 27883): Processes global declarations after optimization\\n- dwarf2out_function_decl (line 28239): Processes function declarations\\n- dwarf2out_source_line (line 29183): Records line number information\\n- dwarf2out_finish (line 32814) and dwarf2out_early_finish (line 33599): Complete debug generation\\n\\n## DIE (Debug Information Entry) Creation\\nThe core of debug information consists of DIE structures. The die_struct is defined in gcc/dwarf2out.cc (lines 3146-3175) and typedef'd as die_node (line 3175). Each DIE represents a language construct (type, variable, function, etc.).\\n\\nDIEs are created by new_die() (gcc/dwarf2out.cc line 5863) and new_die_raw() (line 5850). The new_die function allocates a die_node structure, sets its tag (DW_TAG_*), and links it into the DIE tree by calling add_child_die().\\n\\nAttributes are added to DIEs via add_dwarf_attr() (gcc/dwarf2out.cc line 4497) and various specialized functions like add_AT_flag, add_AT_string, add_AT_die_ref, etc.\\n\\n## Compilation Unit Structure (gcc/dwarf2out.h)\\nThe gcc/dwarf2out.h header file defines key types:\\n- dw_die_ref (line 25): Typedef for pointer to die_struct\\n- dw_attr_node: Attributes attached to DIEs\\n- dw_val_node: Values for attributes (strings, integers, references, locations, etc.)\\n\\n## Generation Functions\\nThe gen_* family of functions in gcc/dwarf2out.cc create DIEs for different language constructs:\\n\\n- gen_decl_die() (line 27537): Generates DIEs for declarations (variables, functions, types)\\n- gen_type_die() (line 27004) and gen_type_die_with_usage() (line 26764): Generate DIEs for types\\n- gen_subprogram_die() (line 23937): Generates function/subprogram DIEs\\n- gen_type_die_for_member() (line 23634): Generates DIEs for class/struct members\\n\\nThese functions call each other recursively to build complete debug information structures, emitting DIEs for nested types, parameters, and local variables.\\n\\n## Line Number Table Emission\\nLine number information is handled by:\\n\\n- dwarf2out_source_line() (line 29183): Records source line/column information for instructions\\n- dw_line_info_table (line 3061): Data structure holding line number entries\\n- dw_line_info_entry (line 3055): Individual line number records\\n- output_line_info() (line 13137): Emits the complete .debug_line section\\n- output_one_line_info_table() (line 12982): Emits individual line info tables\\n\\nThe line number table uses DWARF line number program opcodes to efficiently encode source locations.\\n\\n## Assembly Output (gcc/dwarf2asm.cc and gcc/dwarf2asm.h)\\nThe dwarf2asm module provides low-level assembly output functions:\\n- dw2_assemble_integer() (line 47): Outputs DWARF values as assembly\\n- dw2_asm_output_data(): Macro for outputting DWARF data with labels\\n\\nThese functions are called throughout dwarf2out.cc to emit the actual DWARF sections to the assembly file.\\n\\n## Alternative Output Formats\\nBuilt on top of DWARF DIEs are alternative debug formats:\\n\\n- gcc/dwarf2ctf.cc/h: Generates CTF (Compact C Type Format) and BTF (BPF Type Format) from DWARF DIEs via ctf_do_die()\\n- gcc/dwarf2codeview.cc/h: Generates Microsoft CodeView debug format from DWARF DIEs\\n\\n## Compilation Flow\\nThe complete chain works as follows:\\n1. Front-end calls debug hooks during compilation (via gcc_debug_hooks)\\n2. dwarf2out_early_global_decl/late_global_decl process declarations at appropriate times\\n3. gen_decl_die and related functions create DIE trees for all declarations\\n4. dwarf2out_source_line records line number information for code locations\\n5. output_line_info emits the .debug_line section with line number tables\\n6. dwarf2out_finish writes all remaining DWARF sections (.debug_info, .debug_abbrev, .debug_str, etc.)\\n7. point is the gcc_debug_hooks structure in gcc/debug.h (line 28-210), which defines a set of function pointers called by the front-end during compilation. These include hooks for initializing debug output (init), finishing it (finish), and processing individual language constructs. The gcc/debug.cc file provides default no-op implementations of these hooks.\\n\\n## DWARF Hook Implementation (gcc/dwarf2out.cc)\\nThe dwarf2_debug_hooks structure (gcc/dwarf2out.cc line 2893) implements the debug hooks interface for DWARF output. Key hooks include:\\n\\n- dwarf2out_init (line 30171): Initializes DWARF output structures\\n- dwarf2out_early_global_decl (line 27788): Processes global declarations early in compilation\\n- dwarf2out_late_global_decl (line 27883): Processes global declarations after optimization\\n- dwarf2out_function_decl (line 28239): Processes function declarations\\n- dwarf2out_source_line (line 29183): Records line number information\\n- dwarf2out_finish (line 32814) and dwarf2out_early_finish (line 33599): Complete debug generation\\n\\n## DIE (Debug Information Entry) Creation\\nThe core of debug information consists of DIE structures. The die_struct is defined in gcc/dwarf2out.cc (lines 3146-3175) and typedef'd as die_node (line 3175). Each DIE represents a language construct (type, variable, function, etc.).\\n\\nDIEs are created by new_die() (gcc/dwarf2out.cc line 5863) and new_die_raw() (line 5850). The new_die function allocates a die_node structure, sets its tag (DW_TAG_*), and links it into the DIE tree by calling add_child_die().\\n\\nAttributes are added to DIEs via add_dwarf_attr() (gcc/dwarf2out.cc line 4497) and various specialized functions like add_AT_flag, add_AT_string, add_AT_die_ref, etc.\\n\\n## Compilation Unit Structure (gcc/dwarf2out.h)\\nThe gcc/dwarf2out.h header file defines key types:\\n- dw_die_ref (line 25): Typedef for pointer to die_struct\\n- dw_attr_node: Attributes attached to DIEs\\n- dw_val_node: Values for attributes (strings, integers, references, locations, etc.)\\n\\n## Generation Functions\\nThe gen_* family of functions in gcc/dwarf2out.cc create DIEs for different language constructs:\\n\\n- gen_decl_die() (line 27537): Generates DIEs for declarations (variables, functions, types)\\n- gen_type_die() (line 27004) and gen_type_die_with_usage() (line 26764): Generate DIEs for types\\n- gen_subprogram_die() (line 23937): Generates structures, emitting DIEs for nested types, parameters, and local variables.\\n\\n## Line Number Table Emission\\nLine number information is handled by:\\n\\n- dwarf2out_source_line() (line 29183): Records source line/column information for instructions\\n- dw_line_info_table (line 3061): Data structure holding line number entries\\n- dw_line_info_entry (line 3055): Individual line number records\\n- output_line_info() (line 13137): Emits the complete .debug_line section\\n- output_one_line_info_table() (line 12982): Emits individual line info tables\\n\\nThe line number table uses DWARF line number program opcodes to efficiently encode source locations.\\n\\n## Assembly Output (gcc/dwarf2asm.cc and gcc/dwarf2asm.h)\\nThe dwarf2asm module provides low-level assembly output functions:\\n- dw2_assemble_integer() (line 47): Outputs DWARF values as assembly\\n- dw2_asm_output_data(): Macro for outputting DWARF data with labels\\n\\nThese functions are called throughout dwarf2out.cc to emit the actual DWARF sections to the assembly file.\\n\\n## Alternative Output Formats\\nBuilt on top of DWARF DIEs are alternative debug formats:\\n\\n- gcc/dwarf2ctf.cc/h: Generates CTF (Compact C Type Format) and BTF (BPF Type Format) from DWARF DIEs via ctf_do_die()\\n- gcc/dwarf2codeview.cc/h: Generates Microsoft CodeView debug format from DWARF DIEs\\n\\n## Compilation Flow\\nThe complete chain works as follows:\\n1. Front-end calls debug hooks during compilation (via gcc_debug_hooks)\\n2. dwarf2out_early_global_decl/late_global_decl process declarations at appropriate times\\n3. gen_decl_die and related functions create DIE trees for all declarations\\n4. dwarf2out_source_line records line number information for code locations\\n5. output_line_info emits the .debug_line section with line number tables\\n6. dwarf2out_finish writes all remaining DWARF sections (.debug_info, .debug_abbrev, .debug_str, etc.)\\n7.
